  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b09f07e2-8b9a-4ae4-b714-075ad7fba528'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

Adam is there, poised, threatening to jump. Adam is desperate – but Christine makes a crazy deal with him. His 35th birthday is looming and she bets him she can sh</span>
  <span id="freeText4329168746858339582" style="display:none">She has just two weeks. Two weeks to teach him how to fall in love – with his own life.<br /><br />Adam Basil and Christine Rose are thrown together late one night, when Christine is crossing the Halfpenny Bridge in Dublin. Adam is there, poised, threatening to jump. Adam is desperate – but Christine makes a crazy deal with him. His 35th birthday is looming and she bets him she can show him that life is worth living before then. <br /><br />Despite her determination, Christine knows what a dangerous promise she’s made. Against the ticking of the clock, the two of them embark on wild escapades, grand romantic gestures and some unlikely late-night outings. Slowly, Christine thinks Adam is starting to fall back in love with his life. <br /><br />But has she done enough to change his mind for good? And is that all that’s starting to happen?</span>
  <a data-text-id="4329168746858339582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007350513" href="/book/show/21076159-how-to-fall-in-love">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who want to get in a better mood</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24617462-toni?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099238565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5180879680663105426"><b>
  <i>“You were my wonderfully bespoke original guide to happiness.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>The thing about chick lit is that it's simple. It has cliches, it's highly predictable, but it doesn't make you want to gag. You enjoy it. You expect it. You want it. It can deal with serious topics but not be <i>about</i> them. It doesn't romanticize them.<br/><br/>One of the things this Cecelia Ahern's novel deals with is suicide. Our main character Christine Rossi has witnessed a man kill himself. She tried to help him, but just when she thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText5180879680663105426" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“You were my wonderfully bespoke original guide to happiness.” </i>
</b><br /><br />The thing about chick lit is that it's simple. It has cliches, it's highly predictable, but it doesn't make you want to gag. You enjoy it. You expect it. You want it. It can deal with serious topics but not be <i>about</i> them. It doesn't romanticize them.<br /><br />One of the things this Cecelia Ahern's novel deals with is suicide. Our main character Christine Rossi has witnessed a man kill himself. She tried to help him, but just when she thought she convinced him, she did something wrong. Still getting over the tragedy, Christine crosses the Ha'penny Bridge. And again she sees a man about to jump off the bridge to kill himself.<br /><br /><i>“They say lightning never strikes twice. Untrue. Well,it's true that people say it; it's just untrue as a fact.”</i><br /><br />Christine, desperate to discourage him from taking his life, makes a deal with him: She has two weeks (until his 35th birthday) to prove to him that life is still worth living.<br /><br />I didn't expect to like this book as much as I did. But I read it at exactly the right time. With every adventure Christine and Adam were embarking upon I was getting a little bit better. The book got me half-way out of a terrible mood.<br /><br />I read 3/4 of Cecilia Ahern's other novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17925070.One_Hundred_Names" title="One Hundred Names by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">One Hundred Names</a> in the beginning of last year. I stopped reading it because I started reading other books and then forgot about it. Which is unfortunate because I do remember quite enjoying it. Ahern has a way of writing that is both hilarious and inspirational. Her humor is that kind of humor that you might not laugh out loud to, but you can't help but smile at the <b>freaking wit of the woman.</b> I couldn't keep a straight face.<br /><br /><u>All in All</u>: Whenever you are in a bad mood, I would recommend this book. The experience of the characters feels real even with its cliches. The romance is cute and quite slow burning. It deals with suicide and it doesn't romanticize it. I was delighted.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5180879680663105426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_722914423" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722914423" />
    <a title="Kayleigh {K-Books}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3996633-kayleigh-k-books"><img alt="Kayleigh {K-Books}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540157695p2/3996633.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/722914423?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayleigh {K-Books}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayleigh {K-Books}" href="/user/show/3996633-kayleigh-k-books">Kayleigh {K-Books}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3996633-kayleigh-k-books?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722914423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17416944400265627528"><a href='http://k-booksxo.blogspot.co.uk/2013/09/early-review-how-to-fall-in-love.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>How To Fall in Love Review on K-Books</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"While you were trying to make Maria fall in love with me, and make me fall in love with life, I fell in love with you."</i>
</b><br/> <br/>I have been head over heels in love with Cecelia Ahern right from the moment I started reading her debut novel, <i>PS I Love You</i>, way back in 2007. Ever since then I have obsessed over all of her books and as soon as I heard of this one I was dying to get my hands on it. I pretty much screamed and jumped up and down for a good 10 minutes i</span>
  <span id="freeText17416944400265627528" style="display:none"><a href="http://k-booksxo.blogspot.co.uk/2013/09/early-review-how-to-fall-in-love.html" rel="nofollow noopener">How To Fall in Love Review on K-Books</a><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"While you were trying to make Maria fall in love with me, and make me fall in love with life, I fell in love with you."</i>
</b><br /> <br />I have been head over heels in love with Cecelia Ahern right from the moment I started reading her debut novel, <i>PS I Love You</i>, way back in 2007. Ever since then I have obsessed over all of her books and as soon as I heard of this one I was dying to get my hands on it. I pretty much screamed and jumped up and down for a good 10 minutes in excitement before I calmed down enough to crack open the book and read... and I devoured it in one sitting.<br /><br />Christine has just encountered the most horrifying event. Seeing a man shoot himself in the head changed her life forever. Deciding that she wasn't happy in her life she decided she needed to change before it was too late. After ending her marriage and determined to start again she embarks on a journey she will never forget. Enter Adam. Adam is planning a suicide but Christine stops him from jumping from the Halfpenny Bridge and she promises him that she can help him to enjoy life again. As Christine and Adam are forced together Christine is determined to show him how fun life can be but as they embark on the journey sparks start to fly... can Christine help Adam and let him go at the end? Or are they destined for more?<br /><br /><i>How To Fall in Love</i> is an addictive and heartwarming love story. Cecelia Ahern has blown me away yet again. There's just something about Cecelia's novels where she just brings a little magic into them and they are just like a modern day fairytale. <i>How To Fall in Love</i> is no different. I absolutely adored every single second this book and is just may be my favourite Cecelia Ahern novel to date. It's fantastic. Cecelia's writing style is phenomenal. She pulls you in right form the start and doesn't let you go until well after the story is over.<br /><br /><i>How To Fall in Love</i> is unique, beautiful and uplifting. It is a book that has such a fantastic meaning underneath that it will stay with you long after you have finished reading. It beautiful and magical. It's not just a chick lit love story. The love story isn't the most important aspect of the story. The most important part is showing you that life is hard and though there are many times when we feel like the bad times will never be over we still have to go on. Life is a beautiful thing no matter how difficult it is. Cecelia Ahern is just my hero. I adore her and her novels always have a beautiful uplifting message in them so that when you finish reading you are left feeling like you can face anything.<br /><br /><i>How To Fall in Love</i> is without a doubt one of the best book I have read this year. I devoured the book in one sitting. I just couldn't put it down. It was utter perfection. It was beautiful and moving. Uplifting and Magical. Cecelia Ahern is magical! She is utterly phenomenal and everyone has to read her books. They are perfect and incredible. <i>How To Fall in Love</i> is without a doubt a must-read for everyone. It will make you fall in love and have you wanting to just hug the book forever. I loved every single second of it and I will be waiting on tenter hooks for Cecelia's next heartwarming book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Moments are precious, sometimes they linger and other times they're fleeing, and yet so much could be done in them; you could change a mind, you could save a life and you could even fall in love."</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_781055545" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/781055545" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18012609-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580233082p2/18012609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/781055545?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/18012609-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer781055545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5478312579473778257">How To Fall in Love is Cecelia's 10th book. <br/><br/>This story focuses on Christine Rose, who works in recruitment and has an obsession with self-help books. One night she witnesses a terrible incident with a terrible outcome, and it prompts her to make a life-changing decision. Just a few weeks later, she witnesses a similar terrible incident, but this time the outcome is different. She befriends Adam, a troubled man trying to win his ex-girlfriend back. Christine immediately takes it upon herself to "</span>
  <span id="freeText5478312579473778257" style="display:none">How To Fall in Love is Cecelia's 10th book. <br /><br />This story focuses on Christine Rose, who works in recruitment and has an obsession with self-help books. One night she witnesses a terrible incident with a terrible outcome, and it prompts her to make a life-changing decision. Just a few weeks later, she witnesses a similar terrible incident, but this time the outcome is different. She befriends Adam, a troubled man trying to win his ex-girlfriend back. Christine immediately takes it upon herself to "fix" his situation - essentially giving herself two weeks to show a man how to love life again.<br /><br />I'm used to Cecelia's somewhat juvenile style of writing, which is okay. I expect that from her books - I crave it sometimes when I've been on a crime binge, it's like putting on a pair of fluffy socks. I'm even used to insta-romance and "quirky" leads. What I can't get on board with is the notion of someone befriending a complete stranger with obvious mental and emotional issues and basically becoming their shadow. The entire focus is on Adam's mental state, but it's Christine who I find completely unhinged. She makes decisions no rational person would ever make.<br /><br />The whole story was far fetched, and full of filler - there's an arc about finding out a family secret which has nothing to do with the main story and is never resolved. There's another one involving a detective which we could have happily done without, in particular the chapter about his daughter. I suspect it was the author's way of addressing the recent phenomenon of "slut-shaming", but it came across as 'Oh that would tie in, I'll just whack that in the middle here'. It bore no relevance to the rest of the main characters, and went nowhere. I also thought we had too much of Christine's "bonkers" family. I didn't find them relatable or interesting in any way.<br /><br />Overall, I found the writing childish, the characters unlikeable, the storyline unbelievable, and the main female lead incredibly irritating and irresponsible. I don't even know how to describe it - it's a muddle. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5478312579473778257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1024667605" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1024667605" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1024667605?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007350513" href="/book/show/21076159-how-to-fall-in-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=chicklit">chicklit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1024667605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13608217880701113848"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Cecelia Ahern is one of my favourite authors, and with good reason. She has a way with words. She has a way with taking difficult topics, in this case suicide, and turn it into a book that’s somehow light and makes you smile. There’s always a touch of magic around her stories, something that makes you feel warm and fuzzy inside. And <i>How to Fall in Love</i> is no different.<br/><br/>Christine goes through life swearing by self-help books. How to Fire an Employee, How to Write A Self-Help Book, How to </span>
  <span id="freeText13608217880701113848" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>Cecelia Ahern is one of my favourite authors, and with good reason. She has a way with words. She has a way with taking difficult topics, in this case suicide, and turn it into a book that’s somehow light and makes you smile. There’s always a touch of magic around her stories, something that makes you feel warm and fuzzy inside. And <i>How to Fall in Love</i> is no different.<br><br>Christine goes through life swearing by self-help books. How to Fire an Employee, How to Write A Self-Help Book, How to Enjoy Life. But no book can prepare her when she stumbles across Adam, standing on a bridge and about to kill himself. Christine manages to talk him out of it by promising to show him the beauty of life. She’s given exactly two weeks before Adam tries to kill himself again. So Christine helps him get his girlfriend back, helps him enjoy the little things in life, helps him with family issues. Only things get a little complicated when Christine finds herself falling in love with Adam.<br><br>I have to admit, there were parts that didn’t quite work for me. I thought Christine was sometimes a bit <i>too</i> thorough, walking in on him showering on purpose just to check if he wasn’t trying to kill himself. I get it, he’s suicidal, but there is such a thing as privacy, and some of the scenes felt weird.<br><br>However, once Christine and Adam start to really get along, things are wonderful. There were some scenes that really stood out to me, such as the time when they took a pie baking class together, or the time when Adam dressed up as Where’s Waldo and chased his ex-girlfriend around town with Christine in tow. When there was banter, it was glorious. When a scene had to be cute, it was freaking adorable. I can “complain” about Ahern usually waiting until the very end for the couple to really get together, so about halfway through I found myself looking a little bit like this:<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=jq11c6" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424799283ra/13803613.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But when they do get together, it’s very satisfying. I also really liked Christine’s family – blunt and straightforward to the point of me laughing at pretty much everything they said. They’ll talk about suicide as if you’re talking about the morning weather, and it was hilarious and incredibly refreshing.<br><br>In a way, <i>How to Fall in Love</i> is a self-help book for us too. It’s not just a love story, but it’s a story about how to fall in love with life. It’s sweet, it’s light, it’s fluffy and funny. And you will absolutely fall in love with it.<br><blockquote>
  <i>”Where would we be without tomorrows? What we’d have instead would be todays. And if that was the case, with you, I’d hope for the longest day for today. I’d fill today with you, doing everything I’ve ever loved. I’d laugh, I’d talk, I’d listen and learn, I’d love, I’d love, I’d love. I’d make every day today and spend them all with you, and I’d never worry about tomorrow, when I wouldn’t be with you. And when that dreaded tomorrow comes for us, please know that I didn’t want to leave you, or be left behind, that every single moment spent with you were the best times in my life.”</i>
</blockquote><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13608217880701113848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_831977644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer12438791258562610167">This was my first go with a Cecilia Ahern novel and I feel like writing Cecilia a heart-felt letter of thanks for writing this book. I don't even know where to start except to say I hope to see this on the silver screen soon (I would also be happy to make suggestions on the casting :)) It needs to be a movie.<br/>I had no problems with the book... Nicely paced and she never draws out a scene and make it longer than it needs to be. The characters are relatable and so easy to fall in love with.<br/><br/>I read s</span>
  <span id="freeText12438791258562610167" style="display:none">This was my first go with a Cecilia Ahern novel and I feel like writing Cecilia a heart-felt letter of thanks for writing this book. I don't even know where to start except to say I hope to see this on the silver screen soon (I would also be happy to make suggestions on the casting :)) It needs to be a movie.<br />I had no problems with the book... Nicely paced and she never draws out a scene and make it longer than it needs to be. The characters are relatable and so easy to fall in love with.<br /><br />I read some of the other reviews and I remember there being a few issues with the plot (it not being realistic enough). In my opinion, this is fiction. If it seems too real it would fail completely. And about loose ends (I am reffering to scene with two "Eastern European" men) to me it tied in perfectly with the rest of the book. They were doing something random and then happened upon something random and dangerous... Just as random as finding someone stood upon a bridge ready to jump. Such is the wonder of life<br /><br />Sadly We live in a time where people need grand romantic gestures of love, but living in a world full of malice we easily forget to recognize such things. We forget about the silly things, thinking we need to break out a million candles and spend a fortune on elaborate meals and exquisite jewelery when, in fact, all we need is love... And maybe a lily pad.</span>

        rated it

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007350513" href="/book/show/21076159-how-to-fall-in-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44824883-paul-e-morph?shelf=books-read-in-2017">books-read-in-2017</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1971463379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10200460814743749391">Right, first off, let me just say that I enjoyed this book quite a bit. Cecelia Ahern writes well and has created some engaging characters and interesting scenarios. I do, however, have a couple of criticisms... but I need to hide them due to spoilers:<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[1. The male romantic interest was just SUCH a cliché! He had model good looks, a muscular physique, is independently wealthy yet also has an action-hero job. Talk about the ultimate female wank-fantasy! I could practically hear the b</span></span>
  <span id="freeText10200460814743749391" style="display:none">Right, first off, let me just say that I enjoyed this book quite a bit. Cecelia Ahern writes well and has created some engaging characters and interesting scenarios. I do, however, have a couple of criticisms... but I need to hide them due to spoilers:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. The male romantic interest was just SUCH a cliché! He had model good looks, a muscular physique, is independently wealthy yet also has an action-hero job. Talk about the ultimate female wank-fantasy! I could practically hear the buzz of the author's rampant rabbit every time she described the guy. We are definitely in naked-firefighter-calendar territory here.<br /><br />2. This story is book-ended with two suicide attempts. These two tragic situations are so deeply moving, and the characters involved have problems that were so much more serious and moving than the male lead had, that, unfortunately, the main plot of the book was almost completely trivialised in comparison. To use a phrase from current popular parlance, Ahern (presumably unintentionally) made her male lead feel very much like a 'special snowflake'. I've been told on a number of occasions that I'm a caring, empathic person but even I wanted to give this guy a slap and tell him to buck his bloody ideas up! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />These two issues aside, however, I did enjoy this book. It has some very funny moments and some real emotional highs and lows along the way. I wouldn't let my two criticisms put you off reading it if this sounds like your kind of thing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10200460814743749391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3935451-ririn-aziz?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3935451-ririn-aziz?shelf=my-books">my-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer724125907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1213738233361423602">About a month back, I told a dear friend that the new Cecelia Ahern's book is out and it was called 'How To Fall In Love'. Well, he was amused by it. After reading the synopsis, he asked me,"Can you teach someone how to fall in love? And I'm sure the two main characters will fall in love with each other." Since I haven't read the book at the time, his guess is as good as mine.<br/><br/>So here goes.<br/><br/>How To Fall In Love is the story or rather the journey of two different people, Christine and Adam. Both hav</span>
  <span id="freeText1213738233361423602" style="display:none">About a month back, I told a dear friend that the new Cecelia Ahern's book is out and it was called 'How To Fall In Love'. Well, he was amused by it. After reading the synopsis, he asked me,"Can you teach someone how to fall in love? And I'm sure the two main characters will fall in love with each other." Since I haven't read the book at the time, his guess is as good as mine.<br /><br />So here goes.<br /><br />How To Fall In Love is the story or rather the journey of two different people, Christine and Adam. Both have some issues that were stressing them but ironically that was what bringing them together.<br /><br />Christine was searching for happiness. For quite some times now, she felt lost and empty. She was addicted to self help books or the 'how to' books. After the incident with Simon Conway, she make up her mind to left her husband of less than one year of marriage.<br /><br />Adam was also searching for a way out of all the problems that has been stressing him. He lost the job that he loved due to his father's illness. And when the illness was confirmed as terminal, all his hope to get back the job was crushed, because he has to take his father's place in the family's company, as per his grandfather's will. On top of that, the girlfriend that he hoped to be by his side during this trial has turned to another man, his own best friend.<br /><br />So, it was on that night when Christine was following the instructions of one of her 'how to' books that she met Adam, who was ready to jump into the river at Ha'penny Bridge. Since she cannot save Simon from taking his own life just the week before, she was determined not to let Adam be another one that she will feel guilty about. She just agreed to everything he said, as long as he didn't jump to the river. After it was over, Christine just realised that she had struck a deal with Adam to try to make him fall in love with his life so that he won't feel the urge to take his life again. And if she failed, she has to face the consequence : Adam will take his own life again. And this time, there would be no holding back. The deadline is on Adam's birthday, which is two weeks away.<br /><br />It was during this period that both of them learned some essential lessons about life. There would always be some way to cope with the problems that we faced as long as we opened our heart and mind. There are options for us, not only the obvious one. Life has to be lived to be felt, not just by following the instructions in the books or by taking the easiest way out.<br /><br />So my dearest friend, of course they fell in love with each other, it was a matter of course. But it's the 'how to' that really counts, their journey to find the answers to their quest which led them to the thing that all of us searched for, the contentness with our own life, with someone who loved us by our side, who will always be there for us.<br /><br />'My problem was, I was unhappy with me.You made me like me again. You helped me live my life again. And whether I have you or not, it won’t mean I’ll jump, or end my life. I need to be happy with me. All those things we did for Maria, I enjoyed them because I did them with you. I had fun with you. She may have been the reason, but you were the cause. While you were trying to make Maria fall in love with me, and make me fall in love with life, I fell in love with you.’ - Adam</span>
  <a data-text-id="1213738233361423602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1933231942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1933231942" />
    <a title="Lili  Marcus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58341705-lili-marcus"><img alt="Lili  Marcus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578217505p2/58341705.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1933231942?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lili  Marcus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lili  Marcus" href="/user/show/58341705-lili-marcus">Lili  Marcus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58341705-lili-marcus?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58341705-lili-marcus?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1933231942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7920320085549674740">I've been reading Ahern's works since forever and I love her novels because they're all heartwarming and easy reads. This one isn't different from all her works. I enjoyed it as much as I did with the others.<br/><br/>The heroine, <b>CHRISTINE</b> is obviously has some issues. Her obsessions with Self-help books shows that she isn't happy or contented with her life. And more importantly she needs help. She is looking for something(not gonna tell you what). But when she accidentally witnessed a guy who committed </span>
  <span id="freeText7920320085549674740" style="display:none">I've been reading Ahern's works since forever and I love her novels because they're all heartwarming and easy reads. This one isn't different from all her works. I enjoyed it as much as I did with the others.<br /><br />The heroine, <b>CHRISTINE</b> is obviously has some issues. Her obsessions with Self-help books shows that she isn't happy or contented with her life. And more importantly she needs help. She is looking for something(not gonna tell you what). But when she accidentally witnessed a guy who committed a suicide, she became more aware of her self-her problems and the things that she must do. One of those things is to get out of her marriage. <br /><br />But her husband just can't get over their sudden separation and kept on pestering her. Christine's life took a little turn when she, once again, witnessed another guy,<b>ADAM</b>, trying to kill himself. Not wanting to commit the same mistake she did with the previous suicidal guy, she did everything to convince the guy not to do <i>it</i>. <br /><br />She succeeded and since that day, Adam and Christine were inseparable. Christine, with the help of her self-help books, teaches Adam to love life again, including getting back his ex. And Adam, he still has his issues. He's depressed but little by little, his improvement is obvious and I remember being glad the way he boomed in the story.<br /><br />My only slight problem is that I wish the book is longer and I want a more-definite ending. I want to see Adam really into counselling with a real Psychologist. I want to see both of them being sweet to each other because they're lovers already. It was a happy ending but I want a longer version of the story.<br /><br />I read this one as I was having a break from writing and it turned out I picked the right book. I needed an easy, loving, heartwarming story. This one is all of those. Though it talks about suicide, it is still an easy read. Not depressing at all.<br /><br />Thumbs up for Ahern.:) :) :)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="7920320085549674740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_775501722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/775501722" />
    <a title="Penny McGill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7033258-penny-mcgill"><img alt="Penny McGill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353779762p2/7033258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/775501722?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny McGill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny McGill" href="/user/show/7033258-penny-mcgill">Penny McGill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7033258-penny-mcgill?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer775501722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13568056499697470606">Almost forgot about this one. I've liked other books by Cecelia Ahern but this one didn't grab me at all. I found the whole idea behind the book to be too contrived (and this is not like me - I believe absolutely anything is possible in a novel) and as such I wasn't really swept away in the Romance of the story. <br/><br/>The main character and her love interest did not pull me in at all. On a few occasions I was frustrated by how she, Christine Rose, seemed to be too critical of her friends and not aware</span>
  <span id="freeText13568056499697470606" style="display:none">Almost forgot about this one. I've liked other books by Cecelia Ahern but this one didn't grab me at all. I found the whole idea behind the book to be too contrived (and this is not like me - I believe absolutely anything is possible in a novel) and as such I wasn't really swept away in the Romance of the story. <br /><br />The main character and her love interest did not pull me in at all. On a few occasions I was frustrated by how she, Christine Rose, seemed to be too critical of her friends and not aware of her own failings. She chose to end her own short marriage and I almost felt as if her ex-husband was fortunate to have escaped her. Other parts of the story were not well-developed and took too much of my kindness to believe. Cecelia Ahern's gift for interesting characters popped through in the friends and family who supported Christine but not the woman herself. Sad to say, I wasn't very fond of her love interest either. Once I finished the book I cheerfully moved on to my next one without a thought for their happiness at all. This is not a good sign, usually I wonder what they'll do next and wish there would be a sequel. Not this time. Giving this book a 2-star rating only.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13568056499697470606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1020021228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1020021228" />
    <a title="KimberlyRose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5209299-kimberlyrose"><img alt="KimberlyRose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551901812p2/5209299.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1020021228?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KimberlyRose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KimberlyRose" href="/user/show/5209299-kimberlyrose">KimberlyRose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5209299-kimberlyrose?shelf=2017-and-older-five-star">2017-and-older-five-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1020021228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1577538189596930894">4.5 rounded up<br/><br/>Speed through this one! Which isn't to say I skim read; rather, I absorbed and reread and squished scenes to my chest in fevered joy. A het romance I liked! Rejoice, me! No Pepto to reduce Nicholas Sparks Vomits required. Sorry, Nick, it's not you: most every mainstream romance makes me grab the pink.<br/><br/>First, let me say, my complaints are three, but only one of them took a half star off: the dreaded narrative technique of *gasp* summary *gasp* for a significant sex scene (a single pa</span>
  <span id="freeText1577538189596930894" style="display:none">4.5 rounded up<br /><br />Speed through this one! Which isn't to say I skim read; rather, I absorbed and reread and squished scenes to my chest in fevered joy. A het romance I liked! Rejoice, me! No Pepto to reduce Nicholas Sparks Vomits required. Sorry, Nick, it's not you: most every mainstream romance makes me grab the pink.<br /><br />First, let me say, my complaints are three, but only one of them took a half star off: the dreaded narrative technique of *gasp* summary *gasp* for a significant sex scene (a single paragraph after all that simmering, subtle, delightful build-up?! You're killing me). I don't want clit juices and tongue pokes, hell no, but... Slow. the Fuck. Down. for this meaningful moment. Jesus. Summarize some other time. The others: richer than J. K. Rowling or Rumiko Takahashi plot device? annoying (threw the fabulous realism ajar just a mite); repeated use of the phrase "I was losing the plot," by the confused heroine? laughed with a word-lover's tinkling wind-chime titter the first time and the forth time, ground my teeth. But those last two, who cares because.... <br /><br />Sugar, this is a superb story. Lit up my day, it did.<br /><br />This story. Such a sensitive, compelling look at happiness and love, life and its meaning. Cliched descriptions, but they are just so bang on--truly. But most especially, it has faces--real, vivid, human, *individual* faces--of people with suicidal thoughts and who perform suicidal acts. And they aren't pitied. Or looked down on. Or shameful. And never weak-minded. They are incredible people, beautiful people, but people who need a hand. The MC is wonderful: unique, approachable, flawed, entirely lovable and beseechingly vulnerable despite her positive "Miss Fix-it" spirit. Narrative techniques are often used skillfully; for example, backstory is revealed through the current story (no please-send-me-back-to-the-present flashbacks to try my patience, thank you god). Each character made me smile for different reasons, and even the most silly behaviour (thinking of her family) has hidden foundations.<br /><br />Fun, silly, vivid scenes on top, but beneath, well, that's another story altogether. And together, we've got the heart of the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1577538189596930894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1994634428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer377479134784655924">This is one of my favourite books read in 2018. On third place, to be more precise.<br/><br/>Christine Rose is a gorgeous and unique character. The story starts in a very intelligent way and captures your interest. You won't realize when all the time runs away and all the chapters will flow in front of your eyes!<br/><br/>There are some characters that are a little quite flat, but even so, you love them (or love to hate them). I really liked the plot. The story starts with Christine meeting a man, Simon, who wants </span>
  <span id="freeText377479134784655924" style="display:none">This is one of my favourite books read in 2018. On third place, to be more precise.<br /><br />Christine Rose is a gorgeous and unique character. The story starts in a very intelligent way and captures your interest. You won't realize when all the time runs away and all the chapters will flow in front of your eyes!<br /><br />There are some characters that are a little quite flat, but even so, you love them (or love to hate them). I really liked the plot. The story starts with Christine meeting a man, Simon, who wants to shoot his brains off with a gun. Christine tries to convince him to not give up on life, and actually manages to do so, until she says something that makes him sad again and he pulls the trigger. So, with this trauma, she continues her life, knowing he is in a coma and can't do nothing about it.<br /><br />So, moving on, on a evening walk, she walks on a bridge, and guess what she sees: a man trying to commit suicide by throwing himself off into the water. So, of course, she tries to convince him to choose life. She finds out that his name is Adam, and word by word, she wins the situation, making him choose life... but, only if she manages to show him how great is life until his birthday, which is in a few weeks. If she doesn't, he will commit suicide.<br /><br />So that is how our story begins! Christine learns a lot about Adam and tries really hard to make his life better and they start doing so many crazy stuff together.<br /><br />I'm not really into romance books, but this one is amazing and I love the author. I want to read everything she wrote. Also, I need someone to help me with something: I heard that this book has a movie adaption, but I can't find it. Does anybody know anything about this?<br /><br />5 stars / 5 for this amazing book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="377479134784655924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14830318942310055662"><i>“You were my wonderfully bespoke original guide to happiness.”</i><br/><br/>This was the first book I read by Cecelia Ahern, but it will certainly not be the last. I've recently wacthed the movie "Love, Rosie" (based on a novel by the same author) so when I saw this book on my local bookstore (which has a super small section of english books) I was rather curious and decided to pick it up. <br/><br/>I adoreeed everything about "How to fall in love". This book was witty, funny, romantinc but at the same time delt with s</span>
  <span id="freeText14830318942310055662" style="display:none"><i>“You were my wonderfully bespoke original guide to happiness.”</i><br /><br />This was the first book I read by Cecelia Ahern, but it will certainly not be the last. I've recently wacthed the movie "Love, Rosie" (based on a novel by the same author) so when I saw this book on my local bookstore (which has a super small section of english books) I was rather curious and decided to pick it up. <br /><br />I adoreeed everything about "How to fall in love". This book was witty, funny, romantinc but at the same time delt with serious issues, and I loved how the author delt with it. It was a rather heavy story at times, very emotional but then it had this "escapades" that I reaaally loved, for example every moment with her family like ever - they were such hilarius characters.<br /><br />I also enjoyed how every chapter title was a "How to..." title, because our main character is obsessed with such books. It was a really nice detail. <br /><br />I loved Adam and Christine. Really liked all of their interactions, and their relationship was super cute. Really loved how everyhting turned out in the end. </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34498804-michelle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34498804-michelle?shelf=book-covers-i-love">book-covers-i-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064576158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13427373649924279113">A touching, romantic, tender story. It was realistic in some ways and also involves an unfortunately common and sensitive topic. <br/><br/>Typically but wonderfully, heartwarmingly chick-lit, with a great structure of plot and subplots, along with some very thought-provoking words and events, this book was a highly enjoyable, captivating, and lovable read for me. Officially added to my favourites! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1803796648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1803796648" />
    <a title="Albertina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48814012-albertina"><img alt="Albertina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498169681p2/48814012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1803796648?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Albertina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Albertina" href="/user/show/48814012-albertina">Albertina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007481583" href="/book/show/22843583-how-to-fall-in-love">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1803796648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7623862011259189193"><i>"You were my wonderfully bespoke original guide to happiness."</i><br/><br/>This book was everything to me. <br/>It has been such a long time since I read a book that made me so, so happy. <br/>So exuberant and joyful and I LOVED these character. <br/>In them I saw scattered pieces of me, and I couldn't help but laugh at them sometimes, those fits of giggles that won't end despite you trying. What I appreciated most was how real Christine and Adam felt. I could've found them on the Ha'Penny bridge in Dublin - I'm sure of it</span>
  <span id="freeText7623862011259189193" style="display:none"><i>"You were my wonderfully bespoke original guide to happiness."</i><br /><br />This book was everything to me. <br />It has been such a long time since I read a book that made me so, so happy. <br />So exuberant and joyful and I LOVED these character. <br />In them I saw scattered pieces of me, and I couldn't help but laugh at them sometimes, those fits of giggles that won't end despite you trying. What I appreciated most was how real Christine and Adam felt. I could've found them on the Ha'Penny bridge in Dublin - I'm sure of it. <br /><br />Christine's way of seeing life and tackling every obstacle in her way was admirable, despite her failing miserably sometimes but still being able to look at the bright side. The fact that she would help a complete stranger (sorrowful, sad, lovely, sexy Adam) with his life, and taking leave from her work to do so, says a lot about who she is.<br /><br />Adam was one of those people whose light had been extinguished, but somewhere deep inside there was still an ember. He was so lost in life; saw only problems piling up and didn't have the energy to start solving them, so that jumping off a bridge seemed like the only solution.<br /><br />Seeing him with Christine, how they would interact and do things together made me appreciate life so much more. I know it sounds preposterous, but it really did. I laughed along with them when they did stupid things, or said funny things (which they did a loooooot) <b>like this:</b><br /><br />"'Oh yeah,' he laughed. 'You know, the way you talk, you turn me on like Irma.'<br /><b>(Irma was this super old love-guru that read books in this very sensual voice that wasn't sensual and flirted with young men like Adam).</b><br />'Irma,' I snorted. 'I can't believe she asked for your number.'<br />'And I can't believe I gave her yours.' <br /><br />I completely lost it here, and laughed for about 2 minutes while I reread these lines. I know that they aren't particularly funny, but it was so unexpected, and so so very funny in the context of everything that had happened up until that moment that it became hilarious.<br /><br />And it was this sudden laughter that came without you knowing it, that just bubbles up to the surface and you can't control it for long. Happened more times than I can count.<br />I feel like I'm so much lighter and happier after this book, it did something to me; made me see things I thought were never there in the first place.<br />It's truly one of my favorite reads these year, absolutely heartwarming and stunning and a way of showing that sometimes you want to fix people because you are broken yourself. You think you can mend their pieces together and make them whole, when really they are mending you too because you couldn't see your own broken pieces in your hurry to fix theirs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7623862011259189193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2295175379741050579">Anything can happen just in two weeks. I laughed and cried at the same time when I read this book. This book was amazing.   <span id="freeText2295175379741050579" style="display:none">Anything can happen just in two weeks. I laughed and cried at the same time when I read this book. This book was amazing. I loved the storyline and the way it was delivered. Thank you for such beautiful story.<br /><br />It started with Christine who wants to help people from suicide. She tried to save someone but she failed. She was haunted by that event. Until one day he met a guy who was standing on top of the bridge at the Ha'Penny bridge and she wanted to save him. That's when she met Adam.<br /><br />Christine and Adam became closer ever since she saved him the night at the bridge. Adam wants her ex girlfriend back together with him and Christine is helping him to get his ex girlfriend back. They started to do so many things in order to get the plan works out. <br /><br />Adam on the other hand has something going on which involves his family drama and he needed to go back to his hometown to meet with his family and he brought Christine along. They spent most of the time together and worked out on their plans to win Adam's ex girlfriend back. Did they succeed?<br /><br />As the friendship between Christine and Adam became closer, they had felt something as the matter of heart. Did they going to be together, did Adam get together with his ex girlfriend and leave Christine? You need to read this book to find out.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book. This is my updated review as I wrote a very short one last time.</span>

<div id="review_2106624159" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2106624159" />
    <a title="Mayar El Mahdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33200029-mayar-el-mahdy"><img alt="Mayar El Mahdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596984639p2/33200029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

I've read a couple of others, with <i>Where Rainbows End</i> being one of my all time favourite books.</span>

  <span id="freeText17902383491644057724" style="display:none">How to fall in love, well as if the title didn't give this book away..<br />I read it, I enjoyed it(ish) maybe only because I like reading Cecelia aherns books in general, there were some funnys which made me laugh out loud and the seriousness gave me good for thought, however I can't help but feel a little let down, I don't feel as though I have finished the book and it feels left open for a part 2! <br />I have questions like<br />Did Amelia find her mom, what happened with Christine and Barry did they sort their divorce out ??<br />She was left with nothing, did she get it back??<br />Was her sister a lesbian lol<br />Catherine???? Did they bother in touch with Christine to see what happened as she was there when he died???<br />Maybe I'm too curious but I would have liked the longer fuller version of the story!<br />Can't help but think that Cecelia sold this book on her name and not the content!!!!</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2485722-stephanie-stepping-out-of-the-page?shelf=suicide">suicide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2485722-stephanie-stepping-out-of-the-page?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739821839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14419531497672005987">How to Fall in Love is a book that, thankfully, has a really exciting blurb on the cover. I openly admit that having read one of Ahern's other books (The Gift) I wasn't overly eager to pick up more of her books, but thanks to the description of this one, I overcame my apprehensiveness and I could not be happier that I did! <br/><br/>I am immediately sold to any book which features characters that are emotionally or mentally troubled, so what could be more appealing than this one? Christine, our protagonis</span>
  <span id="freeText14419531497672005987" style="display:none">How to Fall in Love is a book that, thankfully, has a really exciting blurb on the cover. I openly admit that having read one of Ahern's other books (The Gift) I wasn't overly eager to pick up more of her books, but thanks to the description of this one, I overcame my apprehensiveness and I could not be happier that I did! <br /><br />I am immediately sold to any book which features characters that are emotionally or mentally troubled, so what could be more appealing than this one? Christine, our protagonist, hasn't had an easy time since she met a man called Simon, a man who she believed she had talked down from suicide until he suddenly shot himself in front of her, leaving him in a coma. From that night, almost everything changed for her as she began to live with a feeling of guilt and as she also decided to change her home life, leaving her husband. What happens next is the main focus of this story - As Christine is walking through Dublin, she approaches the Ha'penny Bridge and sees a man, Adam, about to jump. Christine felt as though she failed with Simon and so she wasn't going to let Adam go. Christine and Adam make a deal, Christine has up until Adam's next birthday (only two weeks!) in order to make him love his life, otherwise, he is free to do as he wishes. <br /><br />There is a lot of things that I could go into detail about in this book, because there are a lot of things that happen in the two weeks that Christine and Adam have together. A lot of things that they do are in an attempt to try and get Adam's ex-girlfriend, Maria, to fall in love with him again. Adam planned to become engaged to Maria, but was devastated when he found out that his girlfriend and best friend were having an affair. Christine also helps Adam to try and manage his life, sorting through issues with both the family business and family feuds. Christine herself also faces some inner battles, issues with her ex-husband and still finds time to help her friend both cope with a loss and a life-changing revelation. <br /><br />From the first time that Christine and Adam meet, we know that their relationship isn't going to be easy or 'normal' - Christine has agreed to turn the suicidal Adam into someone happier. There is a slight awkwardness between the two of them, a natural awkwardness, something that you would expect to be there, something that feels so real and which adds a sense of authenticity. There are some truly beautiful moments between the couple and it is hard to pinpoint a favourite scene of mine because all of their time together did seem precious, though I did particularly enjoy the more light-hearted and fun times that they had as they began to relax into each others company. The two characters as individuals were well formed, their personalities were both very level and they both seemed very genuine, but when the two characters were together, they both sparked to life - the chemistry between them was incredible, they complimented each other and definitely had one of the best relationships that I've read. <br /><br />How to Fall in Love is a very appropriate title for this book, this story itself has multiple chapters with 'How To' titles and I really enjoyed the format. At the beginning, Christine is a firm believer that there is a 'How To' self-help book for every topic and for every person - she uses those books as emotional crutches and as guidance for her everyday life and of course, she turns to them when she is trying to help Adam. As Christine helps Adam with each step of his changes, we notice that she is altering both of their lives and the chapter headings cleverly reflect that. The book title is appropriate to both the characters inside and to me, as I most definitely fell in love with both the charming characters and heartwarming story.<br /><br />How To Fall In Love is undoubtedly one of the best chick-lit books of 2013 and one of the best I've ever read. I absolutely devoured this book, though I never wanted it to end. This is a perfect book to pick up and become lost in - you will find your mind wandering off into the captivating Dublin setting with these two characters, willing them on along their journey. I completely, wholeheartedly fell in love with Christine, Adam and their emotional story and I'm sure that they will stay in my mind for quite some time. Needless to say, Ahern has certainly taught me 'How To Fall In Love'.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14419531497672005987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16908240745885763197">1 star <br/><br/>Unpopular opinion: DNF because there're so many things that are fundamentally wrong with this book. Most of those many things, as I came to the realization, seemed to be related to the being of our heroine, Christine Rose. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591514037ra/29607400.gif' width='300' height='160' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Christine is possibly one of the worst characters I've ever encountered in a very long time.   <span id="freeText16908240745885763197" style="display:none">1 star <br><br>Unpopular opinion: DNF because there're so many things that are fundamentally wrong with this book. Most of those many things, as I came to the realization, seemed to be related to the being of our heroine, Christine Rose. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591514037ra/29607400.gif" width="300" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Christine is possibly one of the worst characters I've ever encountered in a very long time. Where do I begin? First, she's incredibly selfish. Hers was the worst kind of selfishness because she didn't even seem to acknowledge it. She married her husband and found him boring, so she filed for a divorce (just because), and then she'd been trying to justify her action by playing victim ever since like, page 1, claiming she didn't know what she wanted. Well played, Christine, have you ever heard the word "communication" and "compromise"?, I guess no. Just played with someone's heart based on whatever you wanted at the time alright. Fucking asshole. <br><br>Second, she lived her life based on how-to books. Dude, seriously...<br><br>Third, she basically fell for Adam almost instantly simply because he was handsome (and rich). I mean, that's the only impression I got from her because it happened so fucking suspiciously easily, Christine. <br><br>Fourth, she's incredibly dull. I mean, we're talking about a person who got married because someone else did it. Who read how-to books and followed whatever things somebody did base on the subject because she wouldn't know how otherwise. Who had zero sense of humor (I find her family, on the other hand, hilarious and charming). This person had neither characters nor imagination. She's a fucking identity thief.....the bland kind!<br><br>Fifth, the last and the worst one. She's one of those people who seemed to jerk themselves off by spreading "kindness". Hah. She did "good things" to feel better about herself without really think of long term consequences or sustainability. I mean, here she followed Adam around instead of getting him to see a fucking professional therapist! And then made him do things based on a fucking paperback how-to books! she was so terrible with people in a way that implied that she never actually cared about humanity before, only imposed kindness on them as a mechanism to make her feel better about herself. That's some psychopath energy right there. Most of the things she made Adam do...left me shivering in cringefest. As if this wasn't enough, she was also stubborn about it as well, insisting that she cared and was kind and did well. Dear lord. <br><br>Trust me, I'm dealing with depression myself. Everything Christine did to Adam made me wanted to die sooner on his behalf. She's a doe-eyed cruelty personified. <br><br>Annnnnnnnnd every friggin time someone mentioned how "kind" Christine was, I just wanna hurl this book across the room because....<br>1.) marrying her husband and keeping his heart hostage because she didn't know what to do with her life wasn't kindness. <br>2.) Leaving the said husband because he bored her (without trying to communicate or anything at all) wasn't kindness. <br>3.) Trying to justify herself by chanting about her boring life with the said husband only to fall for the more handsome guy almost instantly right after separating from him wasn't kindness. <br>4.) Peppering suicidal Adam with "positive quotes" wasn't kindness. <br>5.) Following Adam into the toilet wasn't kindness. <br>6.) Helping him winning Marie back wasn't kindness. <br>It's cruelty sugarcoated with good intention and ignorance. It's manipulation. <br><br>So I guess there's the sixth after all. She's MANIPULATIVE. The innocent kind. Long story short, by being in charge of Adam's life, Christine found her place as a savior - it gave her purpose possibly for the first time ever in her dull, colorless life. I bet she would dump him in no time in the future when Adam regained his former personality. Since Adam wasn't an improved character compared to her. I didn't actually care much about the guy, to be honest. <br><br>Anyway, that's how much I loathe this sorry excuse of a fictional human being named Christine. I DNF this book because I couldn't stand her. She's one dimensional, dull, selfish, manipulative, and dumb. God, I should just get a life and move on.</span>

<div id="review_1930710229" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1930710229" />
    <a title="Zoey River" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22072433-zoey-river"><img alt="Zoey River" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498400817p2/22072433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1930710229?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoey River" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoey River" href="/user/show/22072433-zoey-river">Zoey River</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1930710229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8775903739063536029"><b>My rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>There was absolutely <i>nothing</i> I did not like about this book. <br/><br/>It was such a thought-provoking, emotional, wonderful story of two people who meet in the most of unexpected ways and somehow... unintentionally, fall in love. <br/><br/>But this story is so much *more* than just falling in love. It deals with so many subjects and feelings and sadness and hope. <br/>It's a wonderful story about what it means to be alive. <br/>About how, even in our darkest of moments, even when we can't see it for ours</span>
  <span id="freeText8775903739063536029" style="display:none"><b>My rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><br />There was absolutely <i>nothing</i> I did not like about this book. <br /><br />It was such a thought-provoking, emotional, wonderful story of two people who meet in the most of unexpected ways and somehow... unintentionally, fall in love. <br /><br />But this story is so much *more* than just falling in love. It deals with so many subjects and feelings and sadness and hope. <br />It's a wonderful story about what it means to be alive. <br />About how, even in our darkest of moments, even when we can't see it for ourselves, there is always hope. <br /><br />It's about the power of asking for help when you need it. <br />It's about knowing that, despite everyone and everything in the world, there *is* someone out there who'll listen and help. No matter what. <br />It's about the strength to not give up. <br /><br />This book heavily deals with suicide (both the act and thoughts), mental health and death. I'd recommend anyone who is uncomfortable with the subject to think about whether they feel they're able to read it or not. <br />Because this book is also about life, and love, and friendship, and laugh, and hope. <br />Life is all these things. It's never just <i>this</i> or <i>that</i>. It's a series of moments. Some of them sad, some of them happy. Each moment eventually passes, so when you're sad remember you'll be happy once more. And when you're happy know that you can get through the sad to be happy once more. <br /><br />This is an adult contemporary story (I know, not my usual type of read) about a woman named Christine who, one night, finds herself talking a man off jumping from a bridge. She unintentionally finds herself promising him to show him the beauty of life. And so, with only 2 weeks until the final <b>dead</b>line, Christine must save this strange man's life. All the while falling in love. <br /><br />As someone who once knew a person who committed suicide, I found this book very touching and important to read. <br /><br />I swear, this book isn't all that short and yet I devoured it with hardly any breaks in between. <br />It was just that compelling to read. <br /><br />Also, did I mention it takes place in Ireland (a place I have never been but am totally in love with)? <br /><br />Thank you, Cecelia Ahern, for writing a story I did not want to put down. <br />For writing a story that made me feel light and hopeful inside. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VzJGu0Gdhpk" rel="nofollow noopener">With Love - Christina Grimmie</a><br /><br /><i>'Life is a series of moments and moments are always changing, just like thoughts, negative and positive. And though it may be human nature to dwell, like many natural things it's senseless, senseless to allow a single thought to inhabit a mind because thoughts are like guests or fairweather friends. As soon as they arrive, they can leave, and even the ones that take a long time to emerge fully can disappear in an instant. Moments are precious; sometimes they linger and other times they're fleeting, and yet so much could be done in them; you could change a mind, you could save a life and you could even fall in love.'</i><br /><br /><a href="http://magiverse.blogspot.co.il/2017/03/how-to-fall-in-love-by-cecelia-ahren.html" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was first published on my blog Magiverse (:</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8775903739063536029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
